; File: ECOMast.txt 

; This line translation based upon a consolidated version by Franz Hemmer
; <franz@hemsoft.ping.dk> which was in coordinate notation.
;
; J.E.H.Shaw (Ewart Shaw) <strgh@mimosa.csv.warwick.ac.uk> created the
; original list which was the starting point for Hemmer.
; 
; Opening descriptions are from many sources including "Unorthodox 
; Openings" and "The Oxford Companion to Chess."
;
; Translation to standard algebraic with modifications by Paul W. Onstad
; <70641.3236@compuserve.com>
;
; (modifications and additions I have made are marked "*pwo" -Paul)
;
; Chess reader, ChessU4.exe, may be used to review these lines. (See the
; last paragraph--just below.)
;
; A number of lines have been modified or extended, especially those from
; ECO Volumes B, C, & E.
;
; Recently I spent a fair amount of time in untangling the English. It's 
; better than it was but still has more to go.
;
; I have reluctantly decided to include some "natural lines." These are
; opening lines you won't find in ECO but which are, nevertheless,
; accurate. It is a fact that a good number of ECO lines are never
; played in their historical order but yet their resulting, end positions 
; can commonly be reached.
;
; Observations: most of the modifications I have made to this file
; resulted from conflicts noticed while running PGN classifier
; ECOClass.exe against pre-classified game files--notably those classified
; by ChessBase and Chess Assistant. Chess Assistant does the most accurate
; job and therefore I have used it as the standard when resolving
; conflicts (C.A. also includes line codes). I now also have ECO volumes 
; B, C, & E so I've occasionally found situations where even C.A. is apt to 
; get the code wrong. These I have pointed out with notes. For the most 
; part, C.A. still goes deeper than the majority of lines in this document,
; however, since I base my revisions on variations most often played (esp.
; recent games), lines below might go more deeply than C.A. on a game-by-
; game basis.
;
; Where "ECO," in turn, is a little weak is in its tendency to blur English
; openings (Vol. A) with the lower numbered Vol. E openings--particularly
; the Catalan, Queen's Indian, and Nimzo-Indian. I have an idea that if a
; classification scheme were started today, it would include all these
; openings in a single volume.
;
; (See also notes in the B84/B85 section of this document.)
;
; Note: when I have included line codes (/99), I have tended to favor the
; highest numbered line of the terminal position--even though many matches
; will fall somewhat short of the position. This, I have found, makes it
; much easier to reference the line since the lowered numbered code is
; often associated with one of the "dead-end" variations. The main
; consideration then (with the higher number) is to avoid or remove any
; descriptions which would apply only to the terminal position.
;
; I have "disconnected" a good number of gambits and old/odd openings and
; placed them at the bottom of this file. The reason is that they never
; occur in modern games. They might though for blitz and amateur games and
; can easily be activated by taking out the ";" comment delimiters.
; 
; These lines can be read and checked with chess reader, ChessU4.ZIP.
; If adding a new line, check to be sure it is not already entered
; under another move sequence. This can be done by entering the new line
; at the top of the position-search argument file (default, LinesU4.txt),
; then doing either a simple position search (p)--or the "step-back" (p*)
; position search against _this_ line file.
;
; If you obtained this list independently and would like to use it to
; classify PGN games, download ECOClass.ZIP.  -Paul

B84    Sicilian: Scheveningen (Paulsen), classical variation
1.e4 c5 2.Nf3 d6 3.d4 cxd4 4.Nxd4 Nf6 5.Nc3 e6 6.Be2 a6 7.O-O Qc7 1/2

;---------------B84 vs. B85---------------------------------
;    These two ECOs seem rather poorly distinguished. They include the
; same white and black moves in lines swarming with transpositions. This
; may have not always been the case but it is today with modern lines in
; the Scheveningen.
;    Generally, when a lower and higher ECO are similar, the higher
; contains the main lines, and the lower, variations taking off on their
; own from lower points on the trunk of the main line. This was probably
; the intention of B84 but, unless it contains some odd move like Ndb7, a
; line is just as apt to grow back into the trunk again--or onto a main
; B85 branch from the trunk.
;    Case in point:
; 1*e4 c5 2.Nf3 d6 3.d4 cxd4 4.Nxd4 Nf6 5.Nc3 e6 6.Be2 a6 7.O-O Be7
; 8.f4 O-O 9.Be3 Qc7 10.Qe1 b5 11.Bf3 Bb7 12.e5 dxe5 13.fxe5 Nfd7
; 14.Qg3 Kh8 15.Bh5 Kg8   [B85/01, straight book]
; 1*e4 c5 2.Nf3 d6 3.d4 cxd4 4.Nxd4 Nf6 5.Nc3 e6 6.Be2 Be7 7.O-O O-O
; 8.f4 a6 9.Be3 Qc7 10.Qe1 b5 11.Bf3 Bb7 12.e5 dxe5 13.fxe5 Nfd7
; 14.Qg3 Kh8 15.Bh5 Kg8   [B84 or B85?]
;    Both turn out identical but B84/07 is also a good match--at least
; until move 11 (with the absense of 11...exd4). I don't think the ECO
; authors have really figured it out and I know Chess Assistant hasn't
; since it classifies both lines as B84/12.
;    What can be said then is that you will note some conflicts when
; previously classified games are given B84 but ECOClass calls them B85.
; B85 goes deeper though and that has been my criteria. -PWO
;-----------------------------------------------------------
